# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

51-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer file documenting the leader election implementations across both repositories. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary of Findings

### **Kubernetes - Lease-Based Leader Election**
Kubernetes uses two complementary mechanisms:
1. **Basic Lease Election** (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/`) - Time-based leases with RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration
2. **Coordinated Election** (`pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/`) - Version-aware candidate selection using LeaseCandidate objects

Key failover mechanism: When a leader fails, its lease expires after `LeaseDuration`, allowing other candidates to acquire it. The system uses timestamp-based expiration with clock skew tolerance.

### **etcd - Raft-Based Leader Election**  
etcd uses the Raft consensus algorithm with three layers:
1. **Raft Core** (`server/etcdserver/raft.go`) - Leader detection through SoftState.Lead field
2. **Leadership Transfer** (`server/etcdserver/server.go`) - Explicit transfer via `MoveLeader()` for graceful shutdown
3. **Client API** (`client/v3/concurrency/election.go`) - Campaign/Proclaim/Resign with lease-based expiration

Key failover mechanism: When a leader's lease expires (after its session closes), other candidates' Campaign() calls unblock, triggering automatic re-election.

### **Key Differences**
- **Failover speed**: Kubernetes (15-60 seconds) vs etcd (~150-300ms)
- **Split-brain risk**: Kubernetes (higher, time-dependent) vs etcd (none, Raft-based)
- **Fencing strength**: Kubernetes (weak, clock-dependent) vs etcd (strong, quorum-based)

The answer.json file contains detailed file paths, symbols, call chains, and a comprehensive narrative explanation with code examples.

mechanisms:\\n\\n**1. Basic Lease-Based Election (client-go)**\\nThe core implementation is in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`, which defines the `LeaderElector` class. This approach uses Kubernetes Lease objects stored in etcd with the following key components:\\n\\n- **LeaseDuration**: The duration non-leader candidates must wait before attempting to acquire leadership (typically 15 seconds). This prevents thundering herd when a leader fails.\\n- **RenewDeadline**: The deadline by which the acting leader must refresh its lease before losing leadership (typically 10 seconds).\\n- **RetryPeriod**: The interval for retry attempts (typically 2 seconds).\\n\\nThe `tryAcquireOrRenew()` method (line 432) implements the core election loop:\\n1. If the current node is a leader and the lease is valid, it optimistically updates the lease record\\n2. If not a leader, it checks if the observed lease has expired (line 384) and attempts to acquire it\\n3. The lease contains timestamps (AcquireTime, RenewTime) and transition counters\\n\\nWhen a leader fails, the lease expires after LeaseDuration, allowing other candidates to acquire it. The `release()` method (line 314) enables graceful leadership release by setting LeaseDurationSeconds to 1.\\n\\n**2. Coordinated Leader Election (control-plane)**\\nFor critical components, Kubernetes uses coordinated election via `pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/leaderelection_controller.go`. This uses `LeaseCandidate` objects (v1beta1) that represent candidates competing for a single Lease.\\n\\nThe `Controller` manages:\\n- Multiple LeaseCandidate objects that register as candidates for a Lease\\n- Election logic in `pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/election.go`\\n- Strategy-based selection: `pickBestLeaderOldestEmulationVersion()` (line 29) selects the best candidate based on:\\n  1. Lowest emulation version (line 96)\\n  2. Lowest binary version for ties (line 99)\\n  3. Oldest creation timestamp as final tiebreaker (line 103)\\n\\nThe `compare()` function (line 93) implements version-aware comparison for intelligent failover. Candidates periodically update their `RenewTime` and `PingTime` fields; expired candidates are garbage collected (leaseCandidateValidDuration = 30 minutes).\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism**: When a leader crashes, its lease is not renewed. After LeaseDuration elapses, other candidates can claim the lease. The Controller automatically elects the next best candidate according to the configured strategy.\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd uses the Raft consensus algorithm for leader election, implemented in three layers:\\n\\n**1. Raft Core (server/etcdserver/raft.go)**\\nThe `raftNode` struct manages the Raft state machine. Leadership changes are detected through `RaftReady` messages containing a `SoftState` field. The key election loop (lines 180-206):\\n\\n```\\nrd := <-r.Ready()  // Contains SoftState.Lead (current leader ID)\\nnewLeader := rd.SoftState.Lead != raft.None && rh.getLead() != rd.SoftState.Lead\\nif newLeader {\\n    leaderChanges.Inc()  // Track leader transitions\\n}\\nrh.updateLeadership(newLeader)\\n```\\n\\nEtcd's Raft implementation features:\\n- ElectionTicks: Configurable election timeout (typically 10 ticks)\\n- PreVote: Two-phase voting to minimize disruptive re-elections\\n- InitialElectionTickAdvance: Fast-forwards election ticks on startup to speed initial election\\n\\n**2. Leadership Transfer (server/etcdserver/server.go)**\\nFor graceful failover, the `MoveLeader()` method (line 1243) initiates explicit leadership transfer to a designated member:\\n\\n```\\ns.r.TransferLeadership(ctx, lead, transferee)\\nfor s.Lead() != transferee {\\n    // Wait for leadership transfer to complete\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe `TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown()` method (line 1280) ensures graceful shutdown by transferring leadership before terminating.\\n\\n**3. Client-Level Election API (client/v3/concurrency/election.go)**\\nFor applications needing distributed locks, etcd provides a high-level election API:\\n\\n- `Campaign(ctx, value)`: Candidate participates in election by creating a key with a lease (line 69)\\n- `Proclaim(ctx, value)`: Leader updates proclamation without new election (line 110)\\n- `Resign(ctx)`: Leader releases leadership (line 131)\\n- `Observe(ctx)`: Watch election changes including failover events\\n\\nThe Campaign method uses a transaction pattern (lines 74-76):\\n```\\ntxn := client.Txn(ctx).If(v3.Compare(v3.CreateRevision(k), \\\"=\\\", 0))\\ntxn = txn.Then(v3.OpPut(k, val, v3.WithLease(s.Lease())))\\n```\\n\\nThis ensures atomicity: only one candidate can create the election key.\\n\\nFailover works through lease expiration: when a leader's session is closed (e.g., due to network partition), its lease expires, and `waitDeletes()` unblocks other candidates to retry Campaign().\\n\\n**4. Integration Test (tests/integration/v3_election_test.go)**\\nThe `TestElectionFailover()` function demonstrates the complete failover sequence:\\n1. First leader campaigns and acquires election\\n2. Second leader begins campaign (blocked waiting for leader key deletion)\\n3. First leader's session closes (ss[0].Close() - line 153)\\n4. Leadership lease expires, first leader's key is deleted\\n5. Second leader's Campaign unblocks and becomes new leader\\n6. Third observer can Observe the leadership change\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Time-based lease expiration with timestamp comparison | Raft consensus with quorum-based voting |\\n| **Failover Trigger** | Lease expiration (LeaseDuration) | Raft election timeout (ElectionTicks) |\\n| **Re-election Time** | LeaseDuration (15-60 seconds typical) | ~150-300ms (10 ticks \u00d7 heartbeat interval) |\\n| **Fencing** | Limited (relies on clock synchronization) | Strong (quorum-based consensus) |\\n| **Coordination** | Etcd-stored Lease objects | Embedded Raft state machine |\\n| **Split-Brain Risk** | Higher (time-dependent, requires clock sync) | None (Raft prevents multi-leader) |\\n| **Best For** | Components that can tolerate brief unavailability | Critical data consistency |\\n\\n### Common Patterns\\n\\nBoth implementations:\\n1. Use expiration-based failover (time-based for Kubernetes, Raft-based for etcd)\\n2. Implement graceful shutdown via leadership release/transfer\\n3. Support version-aware selection (Kubernetes candidacy version, etcd Raft term)\\n4. Track leadership transitions for monitoring and observability\\n5. Use distributed locks/leases as the coordination primitive\"\n}\n",

mechanisms:\\n\\n**1. Basic Lease-Based Election (client-go)**\\nThe core implementation is in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`, which defines the `LeaderElector` class. This approach uses Kubernetes Lease objects stored in etcd with the following key components:\\n\\n- **LeaseDuration**: The duration non-leader candidates must wait before attempting to acquire leadership (typically 15 seconds). This prevents thundering herd when a leader fails.\\n- **RenewDeadline**: The deadline by which the acting leader must refresh its lease before losing leadership (typically 10 seconds).\\n- **RetryPeriod**: The interval for retry attempts (typically 2 seconds).\\n\\nThe `tryAcquireOrRenew()` method (line 432) implements the core election loop:\\n1. If the current node is a leader and the lease is valid, it optimistically updates the lease record\\n2. If not a leader, it checks if the observed lease has expired (line 384) and attempts to acquire it\\n3. The lease contains timestamps (AcquireTime, RenewTime) and transition counters\\n\\nWhen a leader fails, the lease expires after LeaseDuration, allowing other candidates to acquire it. The `release()` method (line 314) enables graceful leadership release by setting LeaseDurationSeconds to 1.\\n\\n**2. Coordinated Leader Election (control-plane)**\\nFor critical components, Kubernetes uses coordinated election via `pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/leaderelection_controller.go`. This uses `LeaseCandidate` objects (v1beta1) that represent candidates competing for a single Lease.\\n\\nThe `Controller` manages:\\n- Multiple LeaseCandidate objects that register as candidates for a Lease\\n- Election logic in `pkg/controlplane/controller/leaderelection/election.go`\\n- Strategy-based selection: `pickBestLeaderOldestEmulationVersion()` (line 29) selects the best candidate based on:\\n  1. Lowest emulation version (line 96)\\n  2. Lowest binary version for ties (line 99)\\n  3. Oldest creation timestamp as final tiebreaker (line 103)\\n\\nThe `compare()` function (line 93) implements version-aware comparison for intelligent failover. Candidates periodically update their `RenewTime` and `PingTime` fields; expired candidates are garbage collected (leaseCandidateValidDuration = 30 minutes).\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism**: When a leader crashes, its lease is not renewed. After LeaseDuration elapses, other candidates can claim the lease. The Controller automatically elects the next best candidate according to the configured strategy.\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd uses the Raft consensus algorithm for leader election, implemented in three layers:\\n\\n**1. Raft Core (server/etcdserver/raft.go)**\\nThe `raftNode` struct manages the Raft state machine. Leadership changes are detected through `RaftReady` messages containing a `SoftState` field. The key election loop (lines 180-206):\\n\\n```\\nrd := <-r.Ready()  // Contains SoftState.Lead (current leader ID)\\nnewLeader := rd.SoftState.Lead != raft.None && rh.getLead() != rd.SoftState.Lead\\nif newLeader {\\n    leaderChanges.Inc()  // Track leader transitions\\n}\\nrh.updateLeadership(newLeader)\\n```\\n\\nEtcd's Raft implementation features:\\n- ElectionTicks: Configurable election timeout (typically 10 ticks)\\n- PreVote: Two-phase voting to minimize disruptive re-elections\\n- InitialElectionTickAdvance: Fast-forwards election ticks on startup to speed initial election\\n\\n**2. Leadership Transfer (server/etcdserver/server.go)**\\nFor graceful failover, the `MoveLeader()` method (line 1243) initiates explicit leadership transfer to a designated member:\\n\\n```\\ns.r.TransferLeadership(ctx, lead, transferee)\\nfor s.Lead() != transferee {\\n    // Wait for leadership transfer to complete\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe `TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown()` method (line 1280) ensures graceful shutdown by transferring leadership before terminating.\\n\\n**3. Client-Level Election API (client/v3/concurrency/election.go)**\\nFor applications needing distributed locks, etcd provides a high-level election API:\\n\\n- `Campaign(ctx, value)`: Candidate participates in election by creating a key with a lease (line 69)\\n- `Proclaim(ctx, value)`: Leader updates proclamation without new election (line 110)\\n- `Resign(ctx)`: Leader releases leadership (line 131)\\n- `Observe(ctx)`: Watch election changes including failover events\\n\\nThe Campaign method uses a transaction pattern (lines 74-76):\\n```\\ntxn := client.Txn(ctx).If(v3.Compare(v3.CreateRevision(k), \\\"=\\\", 0))\\ntxn = txn.Then(v3.OpPut(k, val, v3.WithLease(s.Lease())))\\n```\\n\\nThis ensures atomicity: only one candidate can create the election key.\\n\\nFailover works through lease expiration: when a leader's session is closed (e.g., due to network partition), its lease expires, and `waitDeletes()` unblocks other candidates to retry Campaign().\\n\\n**4. Integration Test (tests/integration/v3_election_test.go)**\\nThe `TestElectionFailover()` function demonstrates the complete failover sequence:\\n1. First leader campaigns and acquires election\\n2. Second leader begins campaign (blocked waiting for leader key deletion)\\n3. First leader's session closes (ss[0].Close() - line 153)\\n4. Leadership lease expires, first leader's key is deleted\\n5. Second leader's Campaign unblocks and becomes new leader\\n6. Third observer can Observe the leadership change\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Time-based lease expiration with timestamp comparison | Raft consensus with quorum-based voting |\\n| **Failover Trigger** | Lease expiration (LeaseDuration) | Raft election timeout (ElectionTicks) |\\n| **Re-election Time** | LeaseDuration (15-60 seconds typical) | ~150-300ms (10 ticks \u00d7 heartbeat interval) |\\n| **Fencing** | Limited (relies on clock synchronization) | Strong (quorum-based consensus) |\\n| **Coordination** | Etcd-stored Lease objects | Embedded Raft state machine |\\n| **Split-Brain Risk** | Higher (time-dependent, requires clock sync) | None (Raft prevents multi-leader) |\\n| **Best For** | Components that can tolerate brief unavailability | Critical data consistency |\\n\\n### Common Patterns\\n\\nBoth implementations:\\n1. Use expiration-based failover (time-based for Kubernetes, Raft-based for etcd)\\n2. Implement graceful shutdown via leadership release/transfer\\n3. Support version-aware selection (Kubernetes candidacy version, etcd Raft term)\\n4. Track leadership transitions for monitoring and observability\\n5. Use distributed locks/leases as the coordination primitive\"\n}\n",
